Above them, the Salamis roofs bristled with Hellenic ETA operators and a borrowed DEVGRU det that Drakos dubbed "Echo Cell." Seawolf flight orbited offshore with two MH-60S Seahawks loaded with GAU-21s, guided by an MH-60R feeding Link 16 tracks into the gallery’s secure tablet. A SEAL Mark V fast boat idled near the harbor mouth, timed to sprint if skiffs appeared.

The attack started with power flickers—classic SNAFU. Backup generators kicked in, bathing marble statues in amber. Hunt spotted reflections of laser dots in a display case. "Snipers on the colonnade," he whispered. Leyla flicked her EXACTO canister into standby, but this time she let the Hellenic marksmen take the shot. ETA Sergeant Parisis used his Barrett with Greek-mod guidance rounds to nail the rooftop scouts, each bullet arcing around marble cornices.

Inside, faux caterers wheeled silver carts toward the titanium housings. Athena growled. Hunt flipped the carts, revealing suppressed MP7s and satchel charges. "No negotiations," he reminded the stunned thieves before Barakat double-tapped them. Outside, Seawolf-One called "Winchester GAU," having hosed an approaching RHIB, while Seawolf-Two launched a single Hellfire at a mothership trying to nose into the harbor. The gallery never closed; guests assumed it was an elaborate Greek security drill. By dawn, the housings and rare pistols were safe, and Cedar Coalition had earned direct access to Piraeus Naval Base.

*Illustration: Salamis skyline with Seahawk holding pattern and ETA sniper arcs.*

### 55. Thames Fusepoint
While Athens celebrated, Maya’s feed exploded. IRGC hardliners furious over Ras Kamboni had hijacked a Eurotunnel freight consist hauling beryllium plasma tiles and cryogenic deuterium pellet canisters earmarked for UKAEA’s Culham tokamak campaigns. They seized forty commuters near Stratford, threatening to rupture the canisters and aerosolize activated dust across the Jubilee concourse if Maverick’s diamonds and fusion caches weren’t returned. "They moved hostages into a decommissioned Jubilee line spur," MI5’s Saira Malik briefed. "Tunnel suits them—no air assets, no snipers. They expect negotiation."

Leyla’s answer was simple. "We kill terrorists; we do not negotiate." Hunt mobilized the Athens team, flying overnight to RAF Northolt while Hellenic ETA officers prepped as observers. On the Thames, Royal Marines deployed Black Tide-style RHIB cordons to keep copycats away, while the Metropolitan Police’s SCO19 unit cleared aboveground entrances. Under Stratford, the IRGC splinter used sensor tripwires, but Noura’s humidity gauges doubled as LIDAR beacons, plotting every tunnel dogleg. "Hellfire underground is a no-go," Barakat noted. "We do this with EXACTO and flashbangs."

Hunt split the assault: Yael and MI5 hackers remotely looped CCTV to hide the strike, while Leyla led a four-person element through utility ducts, sugar-gelling hinges on blast doors. Barakat and Saira served as dual JTACs for Seawolf flight loitering above the Thames, ready to dump GAU fire onto any escape vehicles. "Remember FIDO," Leyla whispered over comms. "Drive on, even if the tunnel goes FUBAR."

*Illustration: Stratford tunnel schematic with assault routes.*

### 56. Piraeus Drop
The Stratford raid ended in minutes—flashbangs, suppressed MPX bursts, Athena dragging the ringleader down by the calf—but the fallout pointed back to Piraeus. Intercepted phones proved Maverick’s Greek financier planned to grab hostages at the weapons facility after the London distraction. Hunt refused to wait. He ordered a night assault dubbed "Piraeus Drop," blending Greek ETA, DEVGRU’s Blue Squadron, and MI5’s Thames snipers still in EXACTO mode.

Two MH-60S Seahawks from Seawolf flight thundered over Athens, callsigns Trident-One and Trident-Two, each crew of four juggling GAU-21 suppression, fast-rope insertion, and hoist medevac. An MH-60R prowled higher, AN/APS-153 radar searching for rogue drones while the TACCO pumped Link 16 updates to Maya’s tablet. On the ground, ETA troopers and DEVGRU operators stormed the titanium vault, using Saint Barbara icons as legit cover badges—Greek guards waved them through, honoring the patron saint of artillerists.

The terrorists had wired the vault with IR pressure mats tied to hostage collars. Noura crawled under the vitrines, clipping leads while Leyla guarded with her Barrett pegged to EXACTO green. MI5’s snipers on the roof used their guided rounds to arc through skylight seams, knocking out overwatch gunners without shattering marble statues. When a V-250 armored truck tried to ram the service gate, Trident-One’s crew chief poured GAU fire into the engine block and followed with an AGM-114 that ripped the transmission apart. No hostages died; every hijacker lay dead or zip-tied.

### 57. Attica Ledger
Morning light over Piraeus came with paperwork. Greek auditors documented every recovered diamond, weapon, and titanium brace, stamping "Restored" in both Greek and English for Hunt’s museum record. Leyla uploaded Black Fajr’s ledgers to the Cedar Portal, where whistleblowers flooded the feed with tips about Maverick’s remaining financiers. Tarek arrived with baklava and the news that Greece wanted Hunt on retainer as its official rare-weapons restorer—perfect cover for Book Two’s deep dive into Athens and London.

Maya peppered them with updates: oil markets stabilized after Black Fajr’s demise, but Somali side channels were already probing new choke points. Combined Maritime Forces asked Cedar Coalition to brief them on EXACTO employment at sea, while the Royal Marines requested a joint exercise with Hellenic ETA to codify "Black Tide doctrine." Hunt scribbled these FRAGOs into his notebook, labeling the page BOHICA—because more curveballs were inevitable.

Before wheels-up, the coalition hiked the Acropolis at dawn. Leyla left a Saint Barbara medallion near the Erechtheion, thanking the patron saint for another night without casualties. Hunt stood beside her, eyes on the Aegean shipping lanes glittering below. "Somali pirates gone. Greek node contained. London safe for now," he said. "Next, we chase the diamonds deeper into Europe." Athena barked once, as if to say FIDO—drive on. The team boarded their van, bound for the next run of five chapters.

### 58. Levant Relay
The win in Athens lasted twelve hours. Maya lit up the coalition mesh with a Mossad-origin selector—Jerusalem Circuit himself, the man who once sheltered Hunt in his rare-weapons workshop, now calling in every favor. IRGC Unit 840 planned coordinated truck bombs against Greek shipping houses using cedar crates still labeled with Hunt’s forged restoration stamps. Worse, Tehran’s cut-outs had bribed a Levantine customs officer to route the explosive cargo through Haifa and Piraeus, framing Mossad and Cedar Coalition simultaneously. “They’re aiming to pit us against our allies,” Yael warned. “We take the bait, the corridor collapses.”

Hunt, Leyla, Noura, and Barakat flew to Tel Aviv under antique-restorer visas. In a back room of the Israel Museum, the Jerusalem Circuit slid blueprints of IRGC safehouses across a lacquered table. “Maverick told them you’d blink,” he said. “So we burn their pipeline in one night. Mossad takes the north; your Cedar people take the Gulf. We meet back in Haifa when everyone’s tired and nobody’s left alive.” Leyla and Yael traded a look—Gabriel Alon’s shadow hung over the meeting, minus the art-restorer cover; Hunt had become the antique restorer, Alon the ghost.

The plan: intercept the sabotage crates near Tartus with a joint Mossad–Cedar ambush, then use the seized manifests to justify cross-border strikes on Iran’s Khorramshahr logistics hub. Athena and Thanos received microcams with Mossad encryption; Yael patched Cedar’s mesh into Aman’s SIGINT bubble. “You wanted Mossad in the story,” the Circuit said dryly. “Now you’re in ours.”

### 59. Gilan Net
The ambush began off the Syrian coast. A civilian ro-ro ship named *Gilan Star* sailed under a Georgian flag, carrying crates marked “Restoration Supplies—Piraeus.” Hunt knew his signature on those forged papers—they were copies. Seawolf flight’s MH-60S helos hovered at standoff while an Israeli Shaldag fast boat and a Cedar RHIB sprinted toward the freighter under blackout. Barakat and a Mossad Kidon operative named Yaara boarded first, finding cedar crates packed with Semtex, Iranian-sourced ball bearings, and Quds Force kill-switches. “Proof enough,” Yaara said, snapping photos for the Knesset.

With evidence secured, Mossad opened the Caspian route. The coalition flew to Azerbaijan as antique appraisers, convoying with Mossad’s “Carpet Syndicate” smugglers who ran mahogany chests full of 19th-century rifles. Inside the chests: Link 16 repeater nodes, sugar gel, and EXACTO rounds. They slipped across the Astara crossing at midnight, bribing an IRIB inspector with Ottoman bayonets. Once in Iran, Yaara guided them through orange groves to a farmhouse, its basement buzzing with IRGC engineers machining bomb triggers. The team breached silently—Leyla’s suppressed MPX, Yael’s sapper charges—and left no survivors. “No negotiations,” Hunt echoed. They tagged the site with Mossad’s signature calling card: a burned cedar twig, equal parts warning and joke.

### 60. Khuzestan Cutoff
Phase Two struck Khorramshahr. A U.S. Navy Expeditionary Sea Base in the Gulf launched two MH-60S Seahawks (callsigns Cedar-One and Cedar-Two) plus an MH-60R perched high for radar overwatch. Mossad’s maritime unit Shayetet 13 paired with DEVGRU Blue Squadron, fast-roping onto a riverside depot where Unit 840 stored the remaining truck bombs. Greek ETA observers patched in, eager to see how Cedar and Mossad ran joint ops.

Cedar-One’s crew chiefs opened with GAU-21 belts, shredding gun towers, while Cedar-Two hung back with door gunners ready and Hellfires slung. The MH-60R piped Link 16 tracks into Mossad tablets, calling out IRGC patrol boats creeping from the Shatt al-Arab. Mayer, a Shayetet sniper, used EXACTO rounds from the Seahawk’s cabin to arc bullets down alleyways, knocking RPG gunners before they could aim at the rotors. On the ground, Hunt, Leyla, Yaara, and Barakat stacked with DEVGRU, clearing warehouse bays packed with ammonium nitrate and Semtex. They planted thermite charges on pallets, withdrew, and let Leyla torch the depot. Flames rolled skyward; IRGC quick-reaction units arrived too late, greeted by Hellfire strikes that turned technicals into molten steel.

### 61. Isfahan Mirage
With Khorramshahr burning, Mossad fed intel about a backup program near Isfahan, where Unit 840 technicians repurposed art-restoration studios as bomb labs—mocking Hunt’s cover. Jerusalem Circuit insisted Hunt and Leyla run a throwback op: infiltrate as antique restorers inspecting Safavid blades at Vank Cathedral, then poison the logistics branch from inside. Yaara forged priestly invitations; Yael spoofed RFID badges. They entered the Armenian Quarter with toolkits hiding gas grenades and Saint Barbara icons.

Inside the vault, Noura calibrated a portable EMP pen (Leyla’s earlier gift) to fry the lab’s PLC controllers. Leyla swapped lacquer on a ceremonial sabre with sugar gel that would later liquefy the bomb casings, while Hunt used his sketchbook to map emergency exits. When an IRGC colonel recognized Leyla’s face from Piraeus CCTV, she smiled, muttered “FAFO,” and shot him through the throat before the alarm could sound. Barakat dumped thermite into the server rack, while Mossad’s backstop team outside detonated charges under the colonel’s convoy, erasing the pursuit. They exfiltrated through church catacombs, emerging into Isfahan’s midnight markets as fireworks (cover from Mossad) burst overhead.

### 62. Shadow Dividend
The coalition regrouped in Haifa’s underground rail spur. Mossad analysts laid out the result: IRGC’s European truck-bomb pipeline severed, Khorramshahr depot ash, Isfahan logistics crippled, and Jerusalem Circuit’s network intact. He slid a dossier across the table—intel on a Tehran financier who funded both the diamonds cell and Iran’s Somali proxies. “You gave us attacks in Iran,” he said. “Now we give you the ledger for Book Two.”

Maya confirmed oil futures stabilized again and Greek insurers restarted coverage. Combined Maritime Forces asked for Cedar–Mossad briefings on Link 16/EXACTO employment inside hostile airspace, while NATO invited Leyla to teach sugar-gel sabotage at Oberammergau. Tarek toasted everyone with arak and mint tea. “Iran wanted terror,” he said. “Instead they got BOHICA.”

Before wheels-up, Hunt walked the restored pistols back into the Hellenic vault, leaving a sealed envelope addressed to the Jerusalm Circuit—inside, a Saint Barbara medallion fused to an old Ottoman lock plate. Mossad’s art restorer had inspired him; now Samuel Hunt paid the debt forward. The next five chapters waited in Iran’s shadowed financial alleys, but the coalition had proven they could hit Tehran’s proxies at home and still make curtain call as antique curators.

### 63. Jerusalem Workshop
To pay their Mossad debt properly, Hunt accepted the Jerusalem Circuit’s actual request: restore a tranche of antique weapons bound for Israel’s Independence Hall museum. The mission doubled as diplomatic cover and a chance to write the next Cedar chapter on Israeli soil. The Circuit led Hunt and Leyla through a hidden lift beneath Jerusalem’s Mahane Yehuda market, into a humidity-controlled vault stacked with Sten guns, Ottoman jezails, and Palmach-era Brens—pieces smuggled from Syria’s black market before Damascus fell apart. "These aren’t props," he said. "They’re the story of how we kept the state alive. Don’t just clean them—catalog them for the war we’re still fighting."

Noura built a mobile restoration lab inside a disused streetcar, fitting ultrasonic cleaners, blue-light inspection rigs, and a forge small enough to re-blue corroded barrels. Leyla handled provenance paperwork in Hebrew, Arabic, and Greek, while Yael and the Circuit ran counter-surveillance—Unit 840 had posted watchers near the depot, hoping to catch Cedar and Mossad side by side. In the daylight, Hunt wore magnifiers and cotton gloves, polishing a Palmach Sten while explaining to visiting donors how the alloy mix told an underground tale. At night, he and the Circuit used the same crates to ferry Link 16 relay parts to Haifa, sealing them beneath layers of museum wax so no scanner would notice.

The restoration deadline became a mission clock. Every weapon Hunt finished unlocked another slice of intel from Mossad’s archives: rail schedules out of Tehran, crypto wallets tied to the diamonds cell, safehouses in Izmir. Athena and Thanos patrolled the depot like mascots; Israeli schoolkids petted them, never realizing the dogs’ RFID collars were mesh repeaters feeding Cedar’s portal in real time. When an IRGC spotter tried to crash the depot disguised as a courier, Leyla handed him a clipboard and—once inside—quietly snapped his neck, letting the Circuit stage a heart-attack narrative for the newspapers. "No negotiations," she reminded Yael, wiping oil from her hands.

By week’s end, the restored weapons gleamed in display cases, each tagged with Hunt’s meticulous notes. Israel staged a private viewing on the museum roof: survivors of 1948 held the rifles while Mossad briefed the cabinet on Cedar Coalition’s strikes. The Circuit raised a glass of mint tea. "You restored our history and secured our future," he told Hunt. "If Iran tries again, these walls will remember who stopped them." Hunt left Jerusalem with something rarer than payment—a formal liaison charter giving Cedar Coalition legal cover to operate out of the museum workshop whenever Iran’s terror proxies stirred. The mission to Israel wasn’t just about antiques; it was a standing invitation to strike back from the heart of a city built on restoration.

### 64. Haifa Mesh
Extended stay meant infrastructure. Hunt and Leyla leased a defunct spice warehouse near Haifa Port, converting it into a dual-use restoration studio and ops cell. Mossad’s techs threaded Cedar’s mesh nodes through bundles of antique rifle stocks, creating a “Haifa Mesh” that could broadcast SITREPs even if Unit 840 jammed the airwaves. Yael worked with Israeli cyber units to tunnel Cedar Portal traffic through government dark fiber, while Noura built a portable radiological lab disguised as a polishing booth. She stocked it with mini alpha spectrometers hidden inside polish jars and pipettes labelled as lacquer droppers, giving the studio plausible deniability if anyone cracked open the casework.

Daytime routines kept the cover story alive. Israeli families wandered through the studio, sipping cardamom coffee while Hunt re-blued Palmach Stens and aligned Ottoman jezails on velvet pads. He narrated each restoration like a tour guide—explaining British phosphate coatings, the way sand chewed firing pins, how clandestine Palmach machinists stamped serials to fool the Mandate police. Leyla hosted school groups, turning sugar-gel into “museum wax” for the kids while secretly spooling fiber through floorboards. Athena and Thanos slept beside the benches, their harness antennas quietly feeding mesh packets into the Haifa backbone.

After closing time, the studio became a war room. Tables flipped into ops consoles where Mossad analysts piped Aman and Unit 8200 feeds about Tehran’s latest plots. Yael kept a Link 16 tablet tethered to Seawolf flight, just in case a Seahawk needed a fast refuel at Haifa. Noura’s lab snapped into full radiological mode whenever suspicious cargo rolled off the port; she could swab a crate, run readings, and send Cedar Portal alerts before customs even logged the manifest. “You wanted an extended stay,” Jerusalem Circuit said, pouring mint tea as he watched Hunt polish a Sten. “Now you run a neighborhood. Don’t let the neighborhood burn.”

### 65. Galilee Gate
A warning from Aman: IRGC Unit 840 planned to hit a convoy carrying salvaged Syrian manuscripts bound for Jerusalem. The attack would happen near the “Galilee Gate,” a chokepoint on Highway 85 where cedar trees line the bends. Hunt’s team volunteered to ride shotgun as “restoration couriers,” building a legit reason for their presence. Mossad deployed Sayeret Metkal in overwatch, while Seawolf flight loaned one MH-60S det already in the Med on NATO duty. An MH-60R from HSM-74’s det in Haifa provided Link 16 coverage, a rare sight inland but invaluable for calling air tracks.

When IRGC proxies ambushed with explosively formed penetrators disguised as irrigation barrels, Leyla shouted “SNAFU!” and slammed the armored van sideways while Barakat unleashed GAU-21 fire from the Seahawk above. EXACTO rounds curved through olive groves, knocking mortar teams before they could adjust. Noura and Yael used sugar gel to freeze EFP triggers, then Mossad’s Sayeret Metkal troopers swept the orchard, eliminating survivors. The convoy reached Jerusalem intact, manuscripts and antique rifles unharmed.

Political fallout hit within hours. The Israeli Antiquities Authority publicly thanked “international restorers” for defending the Galilee, while Aman quietly fed Cedar Portal the IRGC phone intercepts harvested from the orchard. Lebanese broadcasters tried to spin the ambush as a false flag until Maya streamed helmet cam footage of the EFP barrels stamped with Iranian procurement codes. Villagers along Highway 85 delivered honey and pistachios to the Haifa studio, calling Hunt and Leyla “the librarians with guns.” The cover story deepened rather than frayed.

### 66. Negev Crucible
Extended stay demanded joint training. Mossad invited Cedar Coalition and DEVGRU Blue Squadron to the Negev for a “Crucible”—days of live-fire drills and counter-missile rehearsals. Israeli F-35 Adirs streaked overhead while Seawolf flight practiced low-level runs over Wadi Paran. GAU-21 door gunners shot steel plates while IR drones acted as enemy missiles. Leyla instructed Israeli commandos on sugar-gel sabotage; Barakat coached them on SNAFU/FIDO shorthand. In turn, Shayetet 13 taught Cedar divers how to board Israeli Dolphin-class subs for future covert insertions.

Midway through the exercise, Aman intercepted Unit 840 traffic: an Iranian missile guidance team had slipped into Sinai, planning to lob short-range rockets at Eilat and blame Palestinian factions. The Crucible turned real. Mossad and Cedar launched a night strike, using the Seahawk det for fast-rope insertions while a Romeobird piped Link 16 updates from 10,000 feet. Israeli F-35s orbited dark, acting as antispoof guardians ready to knock down hostile UAVs. The guided-bullet EXACTO kits let operators drop gunners hiding behind dune ridges; DEVGRU’s Blue Squadron shared spotting duties with Shayetet snipers, trading slang and range cards over encrypted radios. Within an hour, the team destroyed the missile cache, leaving Aman to leak photos of “unknown saboteurs” to deter further attempts. The next morning, the Crucible resumed as if nothing had happened, but every trainee could feel the desert’s heat carrying real powder residue.

### 67. Dimona Veil
Israel quietly asked Cedar Coalition to safeguard a convoy moving replacement graphite tiles and control electronics for the Negev Nuclear Research Center near Dimona. Publicly, Hunt’s team played “restoration critics,” inspecting antique pistols at a Beersheba museum. Privately, they escorted the Dimona convoy, embedding Link 16 pucks in each truck. Seawolf flight provided two MH-60S escorts under Israeli callsigns, while Mossad’s drones tracked IRGC spotters who had slipped across Jordan.

Halfway through the desert, a swarm of quadcopters packed with explosives descended. Leyla triggered Cedar’s mesh: Seawolf-One’s crew chief lit the drones with GAU-21 fire while Seawolf-Two fired APKWS rockets to avoid collateral damage. On the ground, Barakat and Yael used electromagnetic pulse pens to fry the few drones that slipped through. When a unit of Iranian-trained militants attempted to ambush at a roadside rest area, Mossad’s snipers rode the Seahawk’s EXACTO rounds to drop the shooters before their RPGs could fire. During a maintenance halt outside Dimona, Hunt taught Israeli engineers how to inspect antique pistols for stress cracks—cover for Noura to quietly swap radiation sensors in the convoy trucks. The Dimona convoy rolled into the facility unscathed, and Israel quietly issued Cedar Coalition permanent “technical advisor” badges for future nuclear-related movements along with a voucher for unlimited workshop time at the Beersheba museum.

### 68. Jerusalem Accord
Weeks of joint work culminated on the Jerusalem Workshop roof, where the President of Israel hosted a closed-door ceremony. Mossad, Cedar Coalition, DEVGRU, and Hellenic representatives signed the “Jerusalem Accord”—a liaison pact granting Cedar legal status inside Israel whenever Iranian terror threats touched Europe or the Levant. The document, framed between two restored Palmach Stens, recognized Samuel Hunt officially as “Chief Antique Restorer and Field Liaison.”

Speeches followed: Jerusalem Circuit thanked Hunt for “polishing ghosts and hunting monsters.” Maya dialed in from Beirut, announcing that the Cedar Portal would open a Hebrew interface staffed by Mossad alumni. Greek Commodore Drakos toasted via holo, promising Greek yards would host Israeli crews whenever needed. The accord also green-lit a shared ops cell linking Link 16 feeds from Seawolf flights, Israeli air wings, and Greek frigates.

As fireworks cracked over Jerusalem, Leyla whispered, “Extended stay achieved.” Hunt nodded, staring at the Old City skyline. “And now we have a reason to come back any time Iran dreams of terror.” Athena and Thanos dozed by the restored weapons, Saint Barbara icons glinting nearby. Mossad issued keycards granting 24/7 access to the workshop; the President tucked a Saint Barbara icon into his suit pocket as a public hint of the alliance. The Cedar Coalition had become part of Israel’s security fabric, blending art restoration with counterterror muscle—exactly the mission the user demanded.
## Appendix A – Cedar Coalition Dossier

**Samuel “Samed” Hunt** – Former U.S. Army MP/SOF liaison. Strengths: counter-proliferation raids, HUMINT rapport, obsessive site sketches. Carries Saint Barbara icon and sugar-gel cartridges taped under his vest.

**Jerusalem Circuit (ally)** – Quiet Mossad veteran who disguises safehouses as rare-weapons restoration studios and courier fronts. Acts as Hunt’s cultural backstop and occasionally opens his network when Cedar Coalition ops need to ghost through Israel or Cyprus.

**Leyla Farouq** – Smuggler/antiquities curator heading Cedar Coalition logistics. Controls honey-bribe economy, Bedouin convoys, and microdrone fleet. Preferred cover: UNESCO cultural officer or airline crew.

**Dr. Noura al-Hadid** – Nuclear engineer behind modular “hospital cores.” Leads Coalition technical standards, translates improvised sabotage into open-source safeguards. Writes equations on IV poles when bored.

**Lt. Rafiq Barakat** – Jordanian SOF. Provides extraction corridors, Bedouin diplomacy, and interrogation muscle. Thinks in debt ledgers; keeps Hunt grounded with sarcasm.

**Inspector Elena Vassos** – Cyprus Customs / EU anti-proliferation. Weaponizes paperwork, smokes through raids, wears floral armor. Liaison to Interpol and EUCOM.

**Yara Khoury** – Fade Nation hacker-activist. Runs NFT-scraper rigs, blackout-proof mesh nets, Cedar Coalition portal backend.

**Yaara Ben-Tzur** – Mossad Kidon operative; liaison to Cedar during Gilan Net and Isfahan Mirage. Specialist in forged ecclesiastical paperwork and sugar-gel delivery systems.

**Shayetet 13 Det.** – Maritime commandos pairing with DEVGRU on Khuzestan Cutoff; maintain a locker inside the Jerusalem Workshop for amphibious kit storage.

**Seawolf Flight (USN det.)** – rotating MH-60S/MH-60R crews staged off Mediterranean destroyers and expeditionary sea bases; provide GAU-21/Link 16 overwatch for Cedar + Mossad.

**Haifa Mesh Cell** – Hybrid Cedar/Mossad techs running the Haifa restoration studio’s mesh network, radiological lab, and Link 16 tap.

**Supporting Cells** – Server Dust (Tripoli), DGST liaison (Morocco), DGSE listening post (Cyprus), Refugee Medical Corps (cover clinics), Mossad dissidents (monitoring Samir fallout).

## Appendix B – Acronym & Gear Glossary

- **Cedar Crown** – Maverick’s modular reactor blackmail campaign (Phases I–III: Levant, Mediterranean, Sahara).  
- **Cedar Coalition** – Hunt/Leyla/Noura transparency consortium countering Cedar Crown via open data + field ops.  
- **ARAR-TRIDENT Fund** – Talal’s laundering route (Riyadh bank → Turkish fintech → UAE metaverse → Limassol).  
- **Phase Sahara** – Current Cedar Crown push (Casablanca → Nouakchott) masked as industrial filtration shipments.  
- **Borey-12** – VolgaShield “fishing” trawler escorting Cedar Crown convoys.  
- **Guidance Tree** – Reactor control lattice; sabotage via coolant thresholds, thermite rods, sugar-gel intakes.  
- **Sugar Gel** – Noura/Leyla mix that crystallizes in seawater, choking engines stealthily.  
- **Spear Drone** – Carbon-fiber dartline used to sever rudder cables or route payload wires.  
- **Saint Barbara Icon** – Hunt’s talisman / cultural bridge token.  
- **Fade Nation** – Barbershop hacker portal (password rotates with NBA trivia).  
- **DGST** – Moroccan General Directorate for Territorial Surveillance (future partner).
- **MH-60S Seahawk** – Four-crew special warfare workhorse with AN/AAS-44 FLIR, Hellfire pylons, and GAU-21/M240 door guns for convoy escort, fast-rope, and armed overwatch sorties.citeturn3search4turn3search1  
- **MH-60R Seahawk** – Maritime strike variant carrying AN/APS-153 radar, ALFS dipping sonar, and Link 16/Hawklink to pass surface/subsurface tracks directly to escorts.citeturn3search1turn3search3turn3search2  
- **GAU-21** – Recoil-softened .50 cal door gun (≈1,100 rpm) mounted on Seahawk swing arms for long-range suppression during boardings.citeturn3search1  
- **Link 16 / MIDS-JTRS** – Encrypted tactical datalink the Seahawks use to feed video, target tracks, and weapons status back to destroyers and the Cedar portal.citeturn3search1  
- **EXACTO Round** – DARPA’s steerable .50-cal bullet with optical seeker + fin actuators that correct trajectory mid-flight so snipers can hit moving targets in crosswinds.citeturn2search0turn2search3  
- **Haifa Mesh Node** – Cedar/Mossad mesh repeater disguised as antique rifle stock bundles; bridges Seawolf Link 16 bursts into secure fiber leading to the Jerusalem Workshop.
- **EMP Pen (Leyla Mk II)** – Portable electromagnetic pulse wand disguised as a jeweler’s caulk pen; fries Unit 840 drone controllers or IR pressure mats at <2 m.
- **Sugar-Gel “Museum Wax”** – Noura/Leyla adhesive that solidifies into crystalline plugs; used in galleries to freeze EFP triggers, sabotage rockets, or hide Link 16 pucks.
- **FUBAR** – “F***ed Up Beyond All Recognition”; Hunt’s shorthand for when ops go off the rails.  
- **FIDO** – “F*** It, Drive On”; Leyla’s reminder to push through compromised timelines.  
- **FISH** – “F*** It, Shit Happens”; Coalition rule-of-thumb when operating on foreign soil.  
- **SNAFU** – “Situation Normal: All F***ed Up”; Markarian’s default state whenever plans collapse.  
- **BOHICA** – “Bend Over, Here It Comes Again”; how operators describe Markarian’s endless curveballs.  
- **FIGMO** – “F*** It, Got My Orders”; attitude of exhausted fighters already packed for the next theater.  
- **FAFO** – “F*** Around and Find Out”; Leyla’s favorite warning to Cedar Crown goons.  
- **SUSFU** – “Situation Unchanged, Still F***ed Up”; the radio call when stalemates refuse to break.  
- **TARFU** – “Things Are Really F***ed Up”; ops tempo redline between SNAFU and FUBAR.  
- **FUMTU** – “F***ed Up More Than Usual”; alerts the team that routine chaos just escalated.  
- **FUGAZI** – “F***ed Up, Got Ambushed, Zipped In”; Leyla’s label for forged paperwork and bait manifests.  
- **JANFU** – “Joint Army-Navy F***-Up”; shorthand for coalition ROE conflicts.  
- **Blue Falcon** – Cynical tag for collaborators and traitorous insiders who sell out their own.  
- **FRAGO** – Fragmentary Order; the mid-mission plan changes SOCOM keeps sending.  
- **SITREP** – Situation Report; Maya’s periodic updates to allies and portal watchers.  
- **JTAC** – Joint Terminal Attack Controller; the air-ground controller Rhodes keeps on station.

### 64. Haifa Mesh
Extended stay meant infrastructure. Hunt and Leyla leased a defunct spice warehouse near Haifa Port, converting it into a dual-use restoration studio and ops cell. Mossad’s techs threaded Cedar’s mesh nodes through bundles of antique rifle stocks, creating a “Haifa Mesh” that could broadcast SITREPs even if Unit 840 jammed the airwaves. Yael worked with Israeli cyber units to tunnel Cedar Portal traffic through government dark fiber, while Noura built a portable radiological lab disguised as a polishing booth.

Daily routine split between public-facing restoration demos for donors and midnight war rooms. Israeli families toured the studio, watching Hunt re-blue Palmach Stens and align Ottoman jezails while Athena napped beside the benches. After closing, the tables flipped into ops consoles where Mossad analysts piped in status reports on Tehran’s latest plots. “You wanted an extended stay,” Jerusalem Circuit said. “Now you run a neighborhood.”

### 65. Galilee Gate
A warning from Aman: IRGC Unit 840 planned to hit a convoy carrying salvaged Syrian manuscripts bound for Jerusalem. The attack would happen near the “Galilee Gate,” a chokepoint on Highway 85 where cedar trees line the bends. Hunt’s team volunteered to ride shotgun as “restoration couriers,” building a legit reason for their presence. Mossad deployed Sayeret Metkal in overwatch, while Seawolf flight loaned one MH-60S det already in the Med on NATO duty. An MH-60R from HSM-74’s det in Haifa provided Link 16 coverage, a rare sight inland but invaluable for calling air tracks.

When IRGC proxies ambushed with explosively formed penetrators disguised as irrigation barrels, Leyla shouted “SNAFU!” and slammed the armored van sideways while Barakat unleashed GAU-21 fire from the Seahawk above. EXACTO rounds curved through olive groves, knocking mortar teams before they could adjust. Noura and Yael used sugar gel to freeze EFP triggers, then Mossad’s Sayeret Metkal troopers swept the orchard, eliminating survivors. The convoy reached Jerusalem intact, manuscripts and antique rifles unharmed. Villagers along the route cheered the “restorers” who had doubled as QRF.

### 66. Negev Crucible
Extended stay demanded joint training. Mossad invited Cedar Coalition and DEVGRU Blue Squadron to the Negev for a “Crucible”—days of live-fire drills and counter-missile rehearsals. Israeli F-35 Adirs streaked overhead while Seawolf flight practiced low-level runs over Wadi Paran. GAU-21 door gunners shot steel plates while IR drones acted as enemy missiles. Leyla instructed Israeli commandos on sugar-gel sabotage; Barakat coached them on SNAFU/FIDO shorthand. In turn, Shayetet 13 taught Cedar divers how to board Israeli Dolphin-class subs for future covert insertions.

Midway through the exercise, Aman intercepted Unit 840 traffic: an Iranian missile guidance team had slipped into Sinai, planning to lob short-range rockets at Eilat and blame Palestinian factions. The Crucible turned real. Mossad and Cedar launched a night strike, using the Seahawk det for fast-rope insertions while a Romeobird piped Link 16 updates from 10,000 feet. The guided-bullet EXACTO kits let operators drop gunners hiding behind dune ridges. Within an hour, the team destroyed the missile cache, leaving Aman to leak photos of “unknown saboteurs” to deter further attempts.

### 67. Dimona Veil
Israel quietly asked Cedar Coalition to safeguard a convoy moving replacement graphite tiles and control electronics for the Negev Nuclear Research Center near Dimona. Publicly, Hunt’s team played “restoration critics,” inspecting antique pistols at a Beersheba museum. Privately, they escorted the Dimona convoy, embedding Link 16 pucks in each truck. Seawolf flight provided two MH-60S escorts under Israeli callsigns, while Mossad’s drones tracked IRGC spotters who had slipped across Jordan.

Halfway through the desert, a swarm of quadcopters packed with explosives descended. Leyla triggered Cedar’s mesh: Seawolf-One’s crew chief lit the drones with GAU-21 fire while Seawolf-Two fired APKWS rockets to avoid collateral damage. On the ground, Barakat and Yael used electromagnetic pulse pens to fry the few drones that slipped through. When a unit of Iranian-trained militants attempted to ambush at a roadside rest area, Mossad’s snipers rode the Seahawk’s EXACTO rounds to drop the shooters before their RPGs could fire. The Dimona convoy rolled into the facility unscathed, and Israel quietly issued Cedar Coalition permanent “technical advisor” badges for future nuclear-related movements.

### 68. Jerusalem Accord
Weeks of joint work culminated on the Jerusalem Workshop roof, where the President of Israel hosted a closed-door ceremony. Mossad, Cedar Coalition, DEVGRU, and Hellenic representatives signed the “Jerusalem Accord”—a liaison pact granting Cedar legal status inside Israel whenever Iranian terror threats touched Europe or the Levant. The document, framed between two restored Palmach Stens, recognized Samuel Hunt officially as “Chief Antique Restorer and Field Liaison.”

Speeches followed: Jerusalem Circuit thanked Hunt for “polishing ghosts and hunting monsters.” Maya dialed in from Beirut, announcing that the Cedar Portal would open a Hebrew interface staffed by Mossad alumni. Greek Commodore Drakos toasted via holo, promising Greek yards would host Israeli crews whenever needed. The accord also green-lit a shared ops cell linking Link 16 feeds from Seawolf flights, Israeli air wings, and Greek frigates.

As fireworks cracked over Jerusalem, Leyla whispered, “Extended stay achieved.” Hunt nodded, staring at the Old City skyline. “And now we have a reason to come back any time Iran dreams of terror.” Athena and Thanos dozed by the restored weapons, Saint Barbara icons glinting nearby. The Cedar Coalition had become part of Israel’s security fabric, blending art restoration with counterterror muscle—exactly the mission the user demanded.
### 69. Astara Ghostline
The Iran supply disruption plan kicked off in Azerbaijan. Cedar Coalition, Mossad, and Aman engineers boarded a night train in Baku under the guise of antique appraisers delivering restored jezails to Tabriz. Hidden inside the crates: sugar-gel splice kits, EMP pens, and Haifa Mesh repeaters. Yael remapped the Astara rail spur feeding Unit 840’s Khorramshahr depots, while Yaara prepped burner phones to spoof IRIB freight confirmations. When the train rolled into Astara at 0200, Hunt and Leyla slipped into the marshaling yard dressed as maintenance techs, planted sugar-gel inside the traction motors, and synced EMP pulses to fry every IRGC locomotive parked on the spur. Barakat and Shayetet scouts covered them from the treeline, using EXACTO spotters to watch for patrols. By dawn, half the trains were inert metal husks; Tehran blamed “copper shortages,” unaware Mossad had uploaded the sabotage footage to a Cedar dead drop.

### 70. Khorramshahr Heist
With the rail choke in place, the coalition launched a ledger grab in Khorramshahr. Seawolf flight inserted DEVGRU Blue Squadron, Yaara, and Leyla onto a riverside customs office while Haifa Mesh nodes relayed Link 16 feeds. Inside, Unit 840 clerks counted diamonds, cash, and crypto hardware destined for Iranian proxies. Hunt used his restorer cover to claim he was cataloging Ottoman pistols impounded by customs; while guards admired the “historical” pieces, Noura tore open the server racks and piped ledger files into the Haifa Mesh. Barakat planted thermite charges under the vaults, timed to ignite only after the team exfiltrated via RHIB. The haul revealed every Caspian ro-ro manifest, with timestamps and bribe routes.

### 71. Caspian Breaker
Using the Khorramshahr data, Mossad and Cedar orchestrated a Caspian ambush. A Georgian-flagged ro-ro named *Azadi Star* carried false “restoration supplies” but actually hid missile guidance chips. Hunt’s cover as an antique restorer let him call the captain, claiming customs paperwork was wrong; while the crew stalled, Seawolf flight’s MH-60S det and an Israeli Sa’ar corvette boxed the vessel northwest of Baku. Shayetet 13 fast-roped from Cedar-One, stormed the cargo deck, and found crates packed with Quds Force hardware. Leyla marked the crates with Saint Barbara icons so Cedar Portal viewers could see the irony live. Tehran’s state TV called it piracy, but the leaked manifests proved Iran was smuggling terror gear under museum covers. Combined Maritime Forces used Cedar’s footage to justify new interdictions.

### 72. Tehran Ledger
The ledger data pointed straight to Tehran financier Hossein Davari, who laundered diamonds, crypto, and antiquities cash through an art fund. Hunt, Leyla, and Yaara infiltrated Davari’s gallery opening as antique appraisers. They swapped placards on his prized Qajar-era pistols with mini EMP pens, then invited him to inspect the pieces in a darkened room. While Davari admired the “restoration work,” Yael tripped the EMPs, frying his crypto cold wallets and setting off the gallery’s Halon suppression. Barakat and Shayetet operators breached through the loading dock, zip-tied Davari, and exfiltrated him via a fake ambulance. Mossad released a sanitized video of the arrest; Cedar Portal published the full ledger, bankrupting Unit 840’s European network. Iran’s foreign ministry raged, but Davari’s clients saw the proof.

### 73. Portal Surge
In Haifa, the Cedar Portal team launched a Hebrew-language transparency hub hosted inside the restoration studio. Maya, Yael, and Yara went live with a “Portal Surge,” inviting Israeli citizens to upload leads on IRGC procurement while anonymizing them via Haifa Mesh. The first day’s submissions flagged two Lebanese front companies; by nightfall, Mossad already had warrants. Greek, Jordanian, and Israeli leaders held a joint press conference referencing the Jerusalem Accord and the Portal Surge, framing transparency as a deterrent. Hunt watched from the workshop mezzanine, polishing a Palmach Sten while Athena and Thanos dozed nearby. The extended stay had evolved into a permanent alliance: museums by day, counterterror furnace by night, with the Cedar Portal documenting every strike.
### 74. Cedar Target Cell
Haifa’s workshop morphed into a joint target cell. Mossad’s Jerusalem Circuit, Cedar Coalition, and a U.S. liaison from JSOC—the codename “Mariner”—ringed the restoration tables with satellite prints of Iran’s nuclear logistics network. Mariner slid a tablet across the wood scarred by centuries of weapon repairs. “Natanz has backup feed lines through underground service tunnels between Kashan and Aran,” he said. “You give us hard coordinates, we give them to CENTCOM.” Hunt, Leyla, Yael, Yaara, Noura, and Barakat divided the map: Haifa Mesh would ingest drone video, Mossad would provide HUMINT, and the U.S. liaison would shepherd the target packages through strike approval.

They built a Cedar Target Cell SOP. Noura handled isotope sampling, packaging every trace reading in the same ledger format she used for rare pistols. Leyla cataloged each tunnel with Saint Barbara icons as waypoints. Yael assigned Link 16 codes so Seawolf flight and Israeli air wings could mark the routes without cross-talk. “We restore antiques by day,” Hunt said. “At night we restore balance.” Mariner grinned. “Big Navy loves your poetry.”

### 75. Natanz Umbilical
The first target: Natanz’s “umbilical” supply tunnels near Aran o Bidgol. Cedar inserted via the same antique-restorer cover used in Isfahan—this time claiming they were cataloging Seljuk swords at a desert shrine. Mossad smuggled them to a ventilation shaft above the tunnel. Hunt and Leyla rappelled into the shaft with sugar-gel satchels shaped like ceramic tiles, gluing them around fiber conduits feeding Natanz’s cascade halls. Noura’s EMP pen pulsed through the lines, frying PLC controllers miles away. Barakat set a timed thermite charge on a coolant manifold and exfiltrated through a hidden camel route prepped by Bedouin allies.

Aboveground, Seawolf flight orbited with one MH-60R feeding Link 16 updates to U.S. satellites while an MH-60S kept GAU-21 suppression ready in case IRGC trucks rolled in. They never did—the tunnel caved in minutes after Cedar left, sealing the umbilical. Mossad doctored satellite imagery to show “landslides,” buying time until CENTCOM could vet the strike intelligence.

### 76. Iskandariyah Signal
To pinpoint Iranian missile staging, the coalition needed eyes in Iraq. Mossad arranged safe passage with Iraqi Counter Terrorism Service, letting Cedar operate near Iskandariyah industrial zones. Yael and Maya deployed Haifa Mesh repeaters disguised as antique crates in a Kuwaiti customs warehouse, then piped sensor feeds to JSOC analysts. Hunt and Barakat, posing as buyers of Ottoman rifles, toured warehouses where IRGC Quds Force stored guidance packages. They used sugar-gel to freeze hinges, EMP pens to fry truck ECUs, and microcameras to map every bay. When an IRGC major arrived to inspect the cargo, Barakat “accidentally” dropped a crate, spilling fake rifle parts that hid Link 16 pucks. The IRGC major signed the manifest anyway, unaware he’d tagged his fleet with trackers.

Within 48 hours, the Haifa Mesh relayed coordinates of every missile convoy rolling toward Syria. CENTCOM slotted them into the target list. Iraqi CT units raided the warehouses, citing “antiquities violations,” giving Cedar plausible deniability while quietly erasing Unit 840’s Iraqi staging grounds.

### 77. Persian Gulf Pinpoint
The U.S. Navy asked Cedar to mark maritime targets for potential strikes. Seawolf flight embarked aboard an Expeditionary Sea Base in the Gulf of Oman, this time with dual-role Seahawks: one MH-60S fitted with GAU-21s and APKWS rockets, and an MH-60R carrying AN/APS-153 radar tuned to low-observable dhows. Leyla, Yael, and the U.S. liaison Mariner rode along, feeding Haifa Mesh data into the destroyer’s CIC. They shadowed IRGC cargo dhows hauling graphite, beryllium, and centrifuge rotors disguised as HVAC equipment.

At night, Cedar planted spear drones on the dhows’ hulls, each drone streaming Link 16 beacons so Tomahawk strike planners could see live vectors. When one dhow attempted to dump cargo overboard, Seawolf-Two’s door gunner hosed the deck with GAU-21 fire, while an Israeli Sa’ar corvette recorded everything for Mossad. By sunrise, CENTCOM had a dozen GPS-precise targets, each annotated with Cedar Portal photos. “Pick your cruise-missile flavor,” Mariner radioed. “Cedar just plated your meal.”

### 78. Strike Matrix
Back in Jerusalem, the Haifa workshop hosted a secure holo conference with the U.S. National Security Council, Israeli War Cabinet, and Jordanian liaisons. Hunt, Leyla, and the Jerusalem Circuit presented the “Strike Matrix”—a tiered list of Natanz tunnel nodes, Khorramshahr depots, Iskandariyah warehouses, and Persian Gulf dhows, each with Link 16 designators and Saint Barbara-coded backup. Noura walked the NSC through isotope lab readings; Yael explained the mesh architecture; Mariner confirmed the coordinates matched U.S. satellite cues.

The War Cabinet approved joint contingency strikes. The NSC tasked CENTCOM to integrate the Strike Matrix into their OPLAN. Media never saw the meeting, but Cedar Portal posted a redacted version, showing citizens the level of transparency behind future strikes. As part of the accord, Cedar Coalition received a standing invite to the Israeli Air Force target shop, while the U.S. liaison left behind a crate of antique cleaning rods—inside them, hardened comms links. “When Tehran moves, we’re already there,” Leyla said, polishing a Palmach Sten as fireworks from Jerusalem’s Old City lit the Haifa night.
### 79. Ramadan Clock
Ramadan began under a curfew of whispers. Cedar Coalition, Mossad, and the U.S. liaison Mariner synchronized watches to the evening call to prayer; the strike window depended on quiet city streets and predictable schedules. Jerusalem Circuit briefed the team atop Haifa’s workshop roof. “During Tarawih prayers, Unit 840 leadership will meet in Mashhad and Tehran safehouses,” he said. “U.S. carriers and Israeli F-35s will be airborne. Your intel makes or breaks the run.” Hunt marked the strike timeline in his notebook, slotting sugar-gel sabotage, Link 16 updates, and Cedar Portal releases into the lunar calendar. “Strike during Ramadan?” Leyla asked. “We’re giving Iran’s people proof their oppressors use holy months for terror.” Everyone agreed: transparency first, precision second.

### 80. Tarqiyah Decapitation
Code-named “Tarqiyah,” the first strike targeted an IRGC Quds Force villa in Tehran’s Tarqiyah district. Cedar fed live Link 16 coordinates from Haifa Mesh nodes hidden in antique crates at the villa’s neighboring gallery. Yael spoofed the villa’s power grid so the F-35 Adirs’ laser designators could see without tipping off the guards. As Tarawih prayers echoed, Seawolf flight’s MH-60R relayed Link 16 bursts to the Adirs and a U.S. B-2 orbiting offshore. Leyla watched the strike feed via a secure tablet—two SDB II glide bombs punched through the villa’s roof, wiping out the Quds command cell without touching the adjacent mosque. Cedar Portal published a redacted video minutes later, showing the leadership plotting terror during Ramadan. Tehran censored it; the world mirrored it anyway.

### 81. Natanz Breaker
Next, CENTCOM unleashed the “Natanz Breaker.” Cedar’s earlier tunnel sabotage created the opening; now U.S. B-2s and Israeli F-35s flew along the corridors Cedar mapped. Hunt, Leyla, and Mariner sat inside the Haifa workshop, relaying Link 16 updates from their target cell. Noura monitored isotope sensors for downwind contamination. At H+00:10, B-2s launched cratering munitions through the collapsed umbilical; F-35s followed with GBU-53/B bombs, slicing through emergency power nodes. Cedar Portal released a live-text SITREP showing the bunkers collapsing. Mossad kept track of leadership casualties—no civilians harmed, no mosques touched. Ramadan prayers continued while Natanz’s heart stopped beating.

### 82. Quds Fallout
Leadership retaliated with rhetoric; Cedar responded with facts. A Quds Force general fled Tehran for Mashhad. Cedar’s Haifa Mesh sniffed his convoy via trackers hidden inside “restored” pistols. Combined Israeli/U.S. strike aircraft tracked the convoy to a safehouse near Imam Reza shrine. To avoid collateral damage, Seawolf flight inserted Shayetet 13 snipers with EXACTO rounds onto a rooftop. During suhoor (pre-dawn meal), the snipers curved guided bullets through the safehouse windows, killing the general and his lieutenants. The strike required no bombs—just Cedar’s trackers and Mossad marksmanship. Cedar Portal published the general’s ledger, proving he financed terror cells during the holy month.

### 83. Aftermath Accord
When dawn broke over Jerusalem, the Haifa workshop hosted another secure holo conference. Israeli, U.S., Jordanian, and Greek leaders signed the “Ramadan Aftermath Accord,” promising continued transparency for any future strikes. Cedar Portal published an abridged target list showing every site hit—Natanz tunnels, Tarqiyah villa, Mashhad safehouse—along with the legal justifications. Hunt polished a Palmach Sten while Leyla drafted the next Field Notes entry: “Ramadan strikes executed with zero civilian loss.” The U.S. liaison Mariner left behind a crate of antique cleaning rods hiding hardened comm nodes, telling Hunt, “Next time we strike, Cedar Portal publishes the proof before Tehran spins it.” As the Eid crescent approached, the Cedar Coalition had demonstrated that precision, transparency, and allied coordination could dismantle terror networks even during the holiest nights.
### 84. Fallout Net
The Ramadan strikes shattered Iran’s command lattice; now Cedar Coalition and Mossad built the “Fallout Net” to catch every surviving Unit 840 cell. Haifa Mesh pulled in whispers from Beirut to Mashhad. Maya, Yael, and the Jerusalem Circuit cross-referenced Cedar Portal uploads with intercepted Quds chatter, color-coding targets like antiquities catalog entries. Hunt led a Haifa workshop briefing for JSOC, Aman, and Jordanian liaisons, laying out a matrix of remaining financiers, drone engineers, and propaganda officers. “Natanz is down, but the regime still has clerks with laptops,” he said. Leyla assigned Mossad teams to the highest-risk nodes, while Barakat coordinated Jordanian arrests along the desert pipeline. The Fallout Net became a vacuum—every time Iran tried to rebuild, Cedar flagged the attempt before sunrise.

### 85. Mashhad Sweep
Unit 840 survivors fled to Mashhad, hoping the Imam Reza shrine’s sanctity would shield them. Mossad leveraged Cedar Portal footage to prove the terrorists exploited holy sites; Iranian citizens quietly tipped the Fallout Net. Cedar and Mossad launched the “Mashhad Sweep,” posing as restoration consultants inspecting Safavid manuscripts in shrine libraries. While crowds prayed, Leyla and Yaara planted sugar-gel charges on the safehouse circuit breakers, then used EMP pens to fry the communications gear. Shayetet 13 snipers, inserted via Seawolf flight, fired EXACTO rounds from a rooftop, decapitating the cell’s new commander. Iranian pilgrims never saw the shooters; they only saw Unit 840 trucks exploding in alleys, reported instantly on Cedar Portal.

### 86. Qum Silence
Clerical hardliners in Qum attempted to reconstitute leadership by issuing fatwas against Cedar and Mossad. The Fallout Net recorded every sermon. Cedar Portal published translations showing the hypocrisy: clerics calling for terror during Ramadan while hoarding smuggled diamonds. Israeli SIGINT identified the seminary’s hidden server farm. Cedar and Mossad ran “Qum Silence,” slipping into the seminary as antique appraisers to inspect Ottoman calligraphy. Hunt and Noura installed Saint Barbara-triggered EMP nodes inside the server room; Leyla laced sugar-gel around the power bus. At dawn, the EMP nodes detonated, wiping every archive backup. The clerics’ encrypted chats vanished; their followers defected, sending Cedar fresh intel. No bombs, no casualties—just silence.

### 87. Western Brief
With Iran’s leadership decimated, the coalition briefed Western allies. The Haifa workshop hosted a secure session with NATO, EUCOM, and Five Eyes reps. Hunt, Leyla, and the Jerusalem Circuit walked allies through the Fallout Net, Mashhad Sweep, and Qum Silence. U.S. liaison Mariner invited Cedar to Washington for a closed NSC readout, while the UK pledged RAF Rivet Joint coverage for future Iranian transmissions. Cedar Portal released a sanitized “Western Brief” summary, explaining how transparency undercut Tehran’s propaganda. Allied parliaments cited the brief when approving new sanctions against surviving financiers.

### 88. Ashen Corridor  
There was no calm—only a corridor of ash stretching from Natanz to the Gulf. As Eid approached, Mossad and Cedar watched Tehran descend into chaos: IRGC officers defecting, clerical hardliners barricading seminaries, Quds Force remnants torching their own depots. Instead of a celebratory declaration, allied leaders issued a grim communique dubbed the “Ashen Corridor,” warning that Iran’s extremist regime was collapsing into infighting. Greek frigates still escorted tankers; Israeli F-35s still patrolled; U.S. carriers stayed on station. “We dismantled their logistics, not their ideology,” Leyla said, polishing a Palmach Sten while smoke plumes from Tehran flickered on Haifa’s holo wall. Noura updated the Field Notes: “Unit 840 leadership decimated; Fallout Net active; regime in freefall—chaos reigns until a new government rises.” The Cedar Coalition understood the assignment wasn’t over. Transparency and precision had shredded the terror infrastructure, but the vacuum boiled with vengeance. Chaos—not calm—was the price of dismantling the extremist regime.
### 89. Ember Warning
No sooner had the Ashen Corridor declaration gone out than Cedar’s inbox flooded with warnings: radical clerics broadcasting on pirate channels, nuclear engineers defecting to hardline militias, Quds loyalists promising “Eid revenge.” Maya tagged it “Ember Warning.” Haifa Mesh triangulated the broadcasts to a Qom suburb; the Jerusalem Circuit confirmed that Unit 840’s extremists were courting foreign fighters. Hunt convened the target cell and drew a new map. “Natanz is rubble, but their ideology still breathes,” he said. Leyla assigned Mossad surveillance teams, while Yael built filters to flag any mention of centrifuge components on Cedar Portal. The threat loomed—if Iran’s radicals reconstituted the nuclear program, the coalition would need to strike again.

### 90. Basra Fuse
Intel pointed to Basra, where radical smugglers tried to fuse together a new nuclear supply line using Iraqi Shia militias and Iranian engineers. Cedar launched “Basra Fuse.” Posing as antique restorer buyers, Hunt and Barakat met militia middlemen at a date-packing warehouse. While Leyla toured the facility, she planted sugar-gel inside crates labeled “HVAC parts.” Seawolf flight circled offshore with Link 16 feeds, ready to unleash GAU-21 fire if the meet went bad. When the militia leader demanded proof of loyalty, Leyla handed over a Saint Barbara icon fused to a detonator—then walked out. Minutes later, the sugar-gel triggers detonated, incinerating the crates full of centrifuge rotors. Cedar Portal published the footage, showing radicals destroying holy-month donations to hide nuclear contraband. Iraqi militias lost face; Iran’s radical followers lost a supply node.

### 91. Crescent Mirage
Radical clerics attempted to rally followers across the “Shiite Crescent,” broadcasting that Cedar Coalition and Mossad were attacking Islam. Haifa Mesh scraped the feeds, and Maya traced the propaganda to an IRGC media bunker near Damascus. Cedar and Mossad ran “Crescent Mirage,” spoofing the bunker’s satellite uplink with Link 16 bursts so the broadcast instead showed Cedar Portal footage of Iranian leaders plotting during Ramadan. Viewers saw their own clerics colluding with terrorists. When the bunker realized the hack, Seawolf flight guided an Israeli F-35 strike onto the uplink dish, wiping it out without touching the neighborhood. The message was clear: radical propaganda would be replaced with proof of their corruption.

### 92. Telic Vortex
The U.S. liaison Mariner warned of a plot to bomb Western embassies in Amman and Ankara using Iranian-supplied drone swarms. Cedar, Mossad, and JSOC launched “Telic Vortex.” Yael rerouted Link 16 tracks from Seawolf flight to U.S. Patriot batteries, while Leyla and Yaara infiltrated a drone workshop in Ankara under the guise of antique appraisers. They planted EMP pens inside the drone racks and used Haifa Mesh to feed telemetry to CENTCOM. When the radicals attempted to launch their swarm during Laylat al-Qadr, the EMP pens fried the drones; minutes later, Patriot batteries and Israeli F-35s struck the warehouse. Cedar Portal published the drone schematics, showing Iranian serial numbers. Western capitals thanked Cedar publicly; Iran’s regime denied everything as usual, but the proof was already viral.

### 93. Eid Vigil
Eid arrived under vigilance, not celebration. Cedar kept the Haifa workshop lit all night, running the Fallout Net while Athena and Thanos patrolled the roof. Hunt drafted Field Notes: “Threat persists; radicals seek nuclear revival; Cedar vigilance perpetual.” Leyla recorded a video for Cedar Portal, telling Iranian citizens that transparency would continue until the terror regime fell. Mossad and JSOC maintained strike readiness; Seawolf flight remained on call. The final line of the Eid Vigil SITREP read: “Threat to do more damage looms if Iran’s extremist regime persists. Cedar Coalition stands ready—every anthem, every Eid, every night.” Chaos still ruled, but the coalition had turned vigilance into a weapon.

### 94. Haifa Forge
Israel asked Cedar Coalition for more than intel—they wanted new weapons platforms tuned specifically for countering Iran. Hunt, Leyla, and Noura turned the Haifa restoration studio into “Haifa Forge,” a joint lab where antiquities benches doubled as prototyping tables. Mossad engineers rolled in Rafael micro-missile mockups; the U.S. liaison Mariner shipped in 3D-printed inlet structures from JSOC’s stealth teams. Leyla’s sugar-gel formulas became vibration dampers for new drone pylons, while Noura adapted her radiological sniffers into modular sensor pods that could clip onto Israeli loitering munitions. Haifa Mesh nodes streamed design telemetry straight to Israeli defense plants, ensuring every micro-adjustment was logged for Cedar Portal transparency. Israel now had bespoke tools to strike Iran’s underground corridors without waiting for allied shipments.

### 95. Aegean Testbed
To prove the platforms, Israel and Greece hosted “Aegean Testbed,” staging launches off Crete. Cedar helped integrate the new pods onto Israeli F-35 Adirs and Greek Rafales. Seawolf flight provided MH-60S chase ships, collecting Link 16 data as the pods mapped mock Iranian tunnels carved into Cretan cliffs. When the new micro-missiles detonated precise sugar-gel explosive charges, the cliffs collapsed exactly as the Natanz umbilicals had. Greek Commodore Drakos streamed the test to Haifa Forge, where Hunt watched the cliffs fall like dominoes. “Jerusalem Forge meets Aegean test,” Leyla said. “If Iranians rebuild, we drop these pods in Eid-eaters’ laps.”

### 96. Negev Railgun
Israel’s Defense Ministry greenlit a rapid railgun prototype to intercept Iranian drone swarms. Cedar’s antique restoration cover allowed them to work at a Negev ordnance site without raising suspicion. Barakat coordinated Jordanian observers; Yael tied the railgun’s telemetry into Haifa Mesh so Seawolf flight could see the shots in real time. Noura’s EMP pen design became the railgun’s capacitor safety. During the first live fire, the railgun shredded ten surrogate drones, proving Israel could create a point-defense ring over Haifa, Tel Aviv, or Dimona. Cedar Portal published a sanitized diagram, crediting the “Haifa Forge” collaboration and warning Iran’s proxies that every drone swarm now met a railgun on standby.

### 97. Jericho Refit
Finally, Israel asked Cedar to inspect Jericho missile silos for rapid refit. Hunt and Leyla, wearing their antique restorer cover, toured the silo galleries with Israeli Air Force engineers. They documented corrosion, swapped out aging wiring with Mossad-provided harnesses, and installed Cedar’s Link 16 pucks so Jericho launches could coordinate with U.S. and Greek networks if deterrence ever failed. “We’re not triggering strikes,” Hunt said. “We’re ensuring the safety switch works when you need it.” The work gave Israel a fully modernized deterrent without revealing secrets to Tehran. Haifa Forge delivered exactly what the user wanted—new weapons platforms tailored for countering Iran when needed.
### 98. Forge Ledger
Haifa Forge became a ledger as important as any strike matrix. Hunt and Leyla documented every pod, railgun tweak, and Jericho wiring change in a leather-bound book stowed beneath the Palmach Stens. Israel’s MOD demanded it; Cedar Portal required transparency. Noura added isotope-tracking formulas so future engineers could recreate the sensor pods without guesswork. Yael tagged each entry with Link 16 callouts, ensuring any pilot could request a specific Haifa kit mid-flight. Mossad archived copies in case Iran ever claimed ignorance. “This ledger writes fate,” the Jerusalem Circuit said. “If Tehran rises again, we open to page one.”

### 99. Euphrates Lure
Rumors emerged of Iranian radicals rebuilding along the Euphrates in Syria. Cedar ran “Euphrates Lure.” Using Haifa Forge’s new pods, Israeli F-35s dropped sensor packages disguised as river debris. Seawolf flight’s MH-60S relayed the Link 16 feed, showing militants hauling centrifuge parts on pontoons. Hunt and Barakat coached Syrian resistance fighters via Haifa Mesh on how to plant sugar-gel charges along the riverbanks. When the militants tried to reassemble the gear, the charges detonated, sinking the convoy. Cedar Portal published the video with subtitles: “Every river hides a fuse.”

### 100. Red Sea Vault
Iranian proxies tried to smuggle nuclear components through the Red Sea under UN aid covers. Cedar and Mossad ran “Red Sea Vault.” Seawolf flight embarked on a U.S. Expeditionary Sea Base, while Leyla and Yaara infiltrated a Sudanese port, posing as buyers of Ottoman sabers. They planted Haifa Forge sensor pods inside the containers. When the convoy set sail, Israeli Dolphin-class subs picked up the pods’ signals, guiding F-35s to conduct pinpoint strikes that vaporized the contraband on barges far from civilians. Cedar Portal pushed the proof before Tehran could lie.

### 101. Cedar Doctrine
With years of ops stacked up, Hunt drafted the “Cedar Doctrine” for allied war colleges. It combined Haifa Forge’s rapid prototyping, Seawolf Link 16 overwatch, sugar-gel sabotage, and Cedar Portal transparency into one playbook. NATO printed it under a sanitized title—“Joint Transparency Precision”—while Mossad taught it at Glilot. The doctrine warned: any regime planning terror should expect Cedar’s ledger, portals, and mesh to expose them before the first missile flies. Iran’s radicals read it too, seething but powerless.

### 102. Hunt’s Oath
On the Haifa roof, Hunt watched the Mediterranean glow during another Eid vigil. Leyla handed him the Haifa Forge ledger; the Jerusalem Circuit poured mint tea; Athena and Thanos snored by the vent. Hunt recited an oath for the Cedar Portal cameras: “As long as terror regimes threaten nuclear fire, we restore the truth, expose their plans, and build tools for those who defend our allies. We do not seek calm. We impose transparency.” The portal broadcast it in Hebrew, Arabic, English, and Greek. Tehran’s radicals raged, promising revenge. The Cedar Coalition merely opened a new page in the ledger—ready to push fate again.
### 103. Portal Watch
Cedar Portal became the world’s most-watched transparency feed. During Eid week, uploads spiked: Iranian civilians sharing secret police routes, tanker captains flagging suspicious dhows, and Iraqi engineers leaking supply manifests. Maya and Yael built “Portal Watch,” a 24/7 moderation cell inside Haifa Forge. Israeli reservists sat alongside Cedar volunteers, translating Farsi and Arabic in real time while Yaara (Kidon) matched faces to Mossad watchlists. Hunt insisted every lead be tied to a physical site sketch—his notebook filled with new diagrams of Tehran alleys and Hormuz coves. “Every citizen video is a fuse,” Leyla said. “Portal Watch lights the cord.”

### 104. Anvil Syndicate
A shadow banking network calling itself “Anvil” tried to resurrect IRGC finances via crypto mixers in Dubai and Istanbul. Cedar, Mossad, and JSOC launched “Anvil Syndicate.” Leyla and Barakat posed as antique dealers bidding on Ottoman sabers in Istanbul’s Grand Bazaar. Hidden inside their display cases: Haifa Forge signal pods tuned to sniff Anvil’s Wi-Fi tags. When the bankers shifted funds, the pods relayed location data to Seawolf flight, which passed it to a U.S. cyber team. Within hours, the mixers froze; Cedar Portal published the wallet addresses before Tehran could launder another rial. Iranian radicals suddenly found their Eid bonuses missing.

### 105. Haifa Shield
Israel asked Cedar to prototype an integrated “Haifa Shield”—linking the railgun, Jericho safeguards, and new sensor pods into a single defensive network. Noura wrote the software; Yael plugged Link 16 and Haifa Mesh into the IDF’s air picture; Seawolf flight provided airborne testing. During a live drill, Haifa Shield detected a simulated drone swarm, tasked the railgun for close-in shots, and queued Jericho telemetry to alert allies. The exercise proved Israel could fight Iranian salvos even if Cedar Portal went dark. Mossad issued Haifa Forge ID badges stamped “Shield Operator,” granting Cedar permanent access to the defensive grid.

### 106. Atlas Link
Greece, Jordan, and Israel wanted a shared corridor for Cedar ops stretching from Casablanca to Haifa. They created “Atlas Link,” a classified fiber/Link 16 backbone running through Greek frigates, Jordanian desert relays, and Haifa Mesh. Hunt flew to Athens, Mykonos, and Amman under his antique cover to inspect every node, sketching wiring diagrams. Commodore Drakos hosted the signing aboard a Hellenic frigate. “Atlas Link keeps the corridor lit even if satellites fail,” she said. Cedar Portal announced it as a transparency guarantee: whenever extremists threaten nuclear terror, Atlas Link carries the evidence straight to the public.

### 107. Citadel Line
The final act of the current run was “Citadel Line.” Cedar Coalition, Mossad, JSOC, Greek ETA, and Jordanian SOF formalized a standing rapid-response unit stationed between Haifa Forge and Amman. Hunt, Leyla, Noura, Barakat, Yaara, and Maya were dubbed “Citadel Line One.” Seawolf flight kept one MH-60S and one MH-60R on constant alert; Haifa Shield monitored the skies; Atlas Link streamed data to Cedar Portal and allied capitals. During the ceremony, Hunt sealed the Haifa Forge ledger and addressed the cameras: “Citadel Line stands between terror regimes and the innocents they target. We will publish every plot, strike every tunnel, and build every tool our allies need.” Tehran’s radicals posted new threats. Cedar simply logged them and opened a fresh page.
### 108. Night Lance
Citadel Line’s first alert came on a moonless night. Haifa Shield detected a cluster of Iranian Shahed-style drones skimming toward Haifa. Seawolf flight scrambled; the railgun fired a bright arc; Jericho telemetry linked with Atlas Link. Leyla and Yael activated Haifa Forge’s sensor pods, feeding precise trajectories to JSOC’s “Night Lance” strike package—two U.S. F-18s stationed over the Med. In seconds, the drones were vaporized; Cedar Portal posted the radar trace with the caption “Citadel Line denies terror.” Tehran tried to spin it, but the transparent data stuck.

### 109. Mariner Echo
The U.S. liaison Mariner requested a formal joint exercise named “Mariner Echo.” Citadel Line One deployed to a U.S. Expeditionary Sea Base alongside Seawolf flight, DEVGRU, and Shayetet 13. They rehearsed simultaneous raids on simulated Iranian oil platforms, using Haifa Forge pods to mark targets, sugar-gel charges to blow pylons, and Link 16 to coordinate F-35 cover. The exercise cemented Citadel Line’s SOPs and convinced CENTCOM to keep a permanent detachment tethered to Haifa Forge. Cedar Portal released a sanitized video, proving U.S.-Israeli-Jordanian cooperation ran deep.

### 110. Haifa Atlas Summit
Athens, Amman, and Jerusalem hosted the first “Haifa Atlas Summit” aboard a Hellenic frigate. Hunt, Leyla, Noura, Barakat, Yaara, Maya, Commodore Drakos, and the Jerusalem Circuit signed a charter stating that any future Iranian nuclear activity would trigger Atlas Link transparency and Citadel Line deployment. Greek ETA and Jordanian SOF were formally embedded into the Citadel roster. The summit livestreamed on Cedar Portal, showing viewers that Mediterranean allies were fused at the command level—not just in secret.

### 111. Portal Covenant
Citadel Line and allied governments issued the “Portal Covenant”: every strike or arrest would be accompanied by immediate Cedar Portal evidence. U.S. NSC, Mossad, Greek MOD, and Jordanian Palace signed it. Iranian radicals raged, but the Covenant made clear that any terror attempt would be documented before Tehran could deny it. Portal Watch operators celebrated with mint tea; Hunt updated the Field Notes: “Transparency is deterrence.”

### 112. Fury Index
Leyla coined the “Fury Index,” a dashboard inside Haifa Forge measuring Iran’s propaganda volume, crypto transfers, and logistical movements. Atlas Link and Haifa Shield fed the index; if it spiked, Citadel Line mobilized. Eid ended with the index low—but not asleep. Hunt, Leyla, Noura, Barakat, Yaara, and Maya stood on the Haifa roof, Seawolf flight orbiting above. “Until the Fury Index hits zero,” Hunt said, “we push fate.” The Cedar Coalition’s story continued, ready for Book Two’s next theater.
### 113. Caracas Checkpoint
Atlas Link flagged Iranian and Russian money laundering through Venezuelan “art restorations” tied to shadow-fleet oil schemes and Cartel de los Soles narco-trafficking. Hunt and Leyla flew to Caracas under UNESCO cover to inspect colonial muskets. Inside a dilapidated gallery, they discovered crypto wallets hidden in refurbished stocks, ledger entries referencing Russian tanker firms on EU blacklists, and shipping manifests linked to the Cartel of the Suns—recently branded a terrorist outfit for feeding Hezbollah and Tren de Aragua cocaine corridors along the Colombian border. Haifa Forge sensor pods disguised as cleaning rods captured every transfer while Portal Watch cross-referenced the data with U.S. sanctions files. When the IRGC handler arrived with a Russian sanctions fixer and a DGCIM escort, Leyla posed as a curator, slipped sugar-gel into the ledger drawer, and detonated it as soon as the wallet synced. Cedar Portal published the video, the sanctions evidence, and the narco links, exposing the Caracas cell, the Russian partners, and the Cartel de los Soles officers protecting them. Venezuelan reformists quietly thanked Cedar; Tehran, Moscow, and the cartel lost another offshore bank.

### 114. Sahel Reliquary
Intelligence showed radicals smuggling uranium through Sahel “reliquary tours.” Cedar deployed to Niger and Mali, posing as preservationists for Tuareg blades. Noura installed Haifa Forge sniffers inside knife cases, while Barakat coordinated with French Barkhane veterans. When the convoy entered Gao, Hunt and Leyla offered to authenticate the relics. While Iranian couriers watched, the sniffers lit up; Seawolf flight relayed Link 16 data to French drones, which struck the escorting technicals outside town. Cedar Portal released proof the “reliquary” tour was a uranium pipeline. Sahel communities opened real museums afterward with Cedar’s help.

### 115. Strait of Malacca Mint
Iranian proxies tried minting crypto inside Southeast Asian pirate dens using “antique weapon auctions.” Cedar, Mossad, and Singapore’s ISD ran “Malacca Mint.” Hunt and Yaara (Kidon) staged a pop-up exhibition aboard a Singaporean patrol vessel, inviting bidders to inspect Malay kris blades. Hidden cameras streamed every face to Portal Watch. When the Iranian brokers attempted to mint crypto, Singaporean commandos boarded the pirate mothership, while Seawolf flight’s MH-60R fed Link 16 to U.S. P-8s. Cedar Portal published the takedown; ASEAN allies requested Haifa Forge sensor pods for future raids.

### 116. Andes Vault
Peruvian authorities discovered IRGC couriers hiding fissile materials inside Incan artifacts. Cedar flew to Cusco under the restoration cover to inspect the “Andes Vault.” Hunt and Noura used Haifa Forge’s radiological lab to test the artifacts; Leyla planted sugar-gel around the vault’s false floor. When IRGC handlers tried to retrieve the stash, Peruvian commandos—briefed via Atlas Link—sealed the exits. Cedar Portal shared the joint op footage, showing Iran’s extremists desecrating Incan heritage. Peru and Chile signed onto Atlas Link afterward.

### 117. Pacific Relic Run
The final hotspot was the Pacific. Iranian agents attempted to move components via Polynesian “relic runs,” shipping WWII relics between Kiribati and Fiji. Cedar partnered with Australia and New Zealand under the Five Eyes umbrella. Hunt and Leyla joined a museum exchange, inspecting relics aboard a Royal New Zealand Navy vessel. Haifa Forge pods tagged the cargo; Australian P-8s tracked the shipment to a covert Iranian barge. Seawolf flight’s MH-60S escorted Aussie SAS troopers, who seized the barge without firing a shot. Cedar Portal published the evidence; Pacific nations requested Atlas Link access. The restoration cover had become a global network, throttling Iran wherever it tried to hide.

### 118. Shadow Fleet Burn
Iran’s illegal oil sales continued via “shadow fleet” tankers running dark in the Mediterranean and Indian Ocean. Cedar Coalition, Mossad, and Combined Maritime Forces ran “Shadow Fleet Burn.” Under the restoration cover, Hunt and Leyla inspected “antique” engine parts in Greek shipbreaking yards, secretly embedding Haifa Forge beacons into suspect tankers’ ballast pumps. Seawolf flight relayed Link 16 data to U.S. P-8s and French Atlantique patrol aircraft, which tracked the tankers as they conducted ship-to-ship transfers off Malta and Goa. Once the evidence was in hand, EU navies seized the tankers, while Cedar Portal published the transfer logs and AIS spoofing routes. Tehran’s sanction-skirting oil syndicate lost vessels overnight, and insurers blacklisted the rest.

### 119. Operation Southern Spear
Book Two opened with Operation Southern Spear, echoing the real U.S. deployment announced when President Reynolds invoked the Alien Enemies Act against Tren de Aragua. Cedar Coalition embedded into the multinational task force as “restoration advisors” cataloging colonial weapons in Caracas. In reality, Hunt and Leyla mapped Cartel de los Soles safehouses while JSOC Marines staged offshore. Haifa Forge pods tracked the cartel’s narco flights; Portal Watch piped the feeds into OFAC’s sanctions desk. When U.S. Marines hit the Cartel of the Suns’ depots, Cedar streamed proof of the cartel’s links to Iran and Russia, giving Operation Southern Spear political cover worldwide.

### 120. Maracaibo Veil
The cartel shifted toward the Colombia-Venezuela border, hiding under the skyline of Maracaibo. Cedar launched “Maracaibo Veil.” Hunt and Barakat, posing as appraisers of colonial sabers for a Maracaibo museum, used Haifa Forge sniffers to detect cocaine caches laced with Iranian-origin precursors. Leyla coordinated with Colombian Jungla commandos and U.S. Southern Command advisers, sharing Atlas Link telemetry in real time. When Tren de Aragua couriers crossed the Puente Internacional, Cedar triggered sugar-gel charges in their armored SUVs while Colombian police sealed the exits. Portal Watch posted the raid video with overlays showing the cartel’s Hezbollah connections, undermining its propaganda.

### 121. Orinoco Ghosts
Cartel leaders fled into the Orinoco Delta, running narco-submarines escorted by Hezbollah gunboats. When the subs relaunched, the beacons called in U.S. P-8s and Colombian Black Hawks. Sayeret 13 (on loan from Mossad) inserted from Seawolf helicopters, captured the flotilla, and uploaded ledgers proving the Cartel of the Suns financed Iran’s missile programs. Cedar Portal published the evidence within the hour.

### 122. Cartel Gridlock
Next, Cedar helped the Treasury’s Counter-Narcotics Task Force freeze cartel money. “Cartel Gridlock” digitized every seizure from Caracas Checkpoint through Orinoco Ghosts, sending Atlas Link packets straight to OFAC, EU regulators, and Operation Southern Spear. Noura and Maya built dashboards showing how each art-restoration cover exposed narco-shell companies in Panama, Curacao, and Moscow. Hunt briefed the White House and NATO on the new doctrine: restoration missions paired with sanctions data. Cedar Portal released a public version, letting citizens track sanctioned vessels, banks, and Cartel de los Soles officers in real time.

### 123. Condor Lance
The final mission in the opening narco arc, “Condor Lance,” took Citadel Line to the Andes. Iranian facilitators tried to reopen the Andes Vault using Bolivian airstrips and narco pilots. Cedar teamed with Peruvian and Chilean special forces, embedding as antique restoration experts cataloging Incan gold. ### 124. Colombia Interdiction
Cartel de los Soles runners shifted cocaine and Iranian precursors through the Guajira desert into Colombia. Cedar launched “Colombia Interdiction,” partnering with Colombian Jungla units and U.S. DEA FAST teams. ### 125. Darién Snare
Tren de Aragua couriers tried to exploit the Darién Gap migrant routes. Cedar’s “Darién Snare” mission embedded with Panamanian SENAFRONT units. ### 126. Panama Ledger
The cartel funneled money through Panama City art auctions. “Panama Ledger” saw Leyla and Noura pose as museum conservators, using Haifa Forge pods to monitor every bidder’s crypto wallet. Atlas Link fed the data to OFAC, Operation Southern Spear, and Interpol. When a Venezuelan banker tried to launder $100 million for Tehran’s missile bureau, Panamanian police—coached by Cedar—froze the funds live on camera. ### 127. Caribbean Shield
Cartel leaders fled toward island havens, hiding within Trinidad-Tobago petro hubs.
